<p>The <b>Caspian Sea</b> is the world's largest inland <a href="/wiki/Body_of_water" title="Body of water">body of water</a>, often described as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_by_area" title="List of lakes by area">world's largest lake</a> or a full-fledged sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">endorheic basin</a>, it lies between Europe and Asia; east of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, west of the broad <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, south of the fertile plains of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Russia" title="Southern Russia">Southern Russia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, and north of the mountainous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_Plateau" title="Iranian Plateau">Iranian Plateau</a> of <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>. It covers 143,550 sq mi (372,000 km<sup>2</sup>) (excluding the highly saline lagoon of <a href="/wiki/Garabogazk%C3%B6l" title="Garabogazköl">Garabogazköl</a> to its east) and a volume of 78,200 km<sup>3</sup> (19,000 cu mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> It has a <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">salinity</a> of approximately 1.2% (12 g/L), about a third of the salinity of average <a href="/wiki/Seawater" title="Seawater">seawater</a>. It is bounded by <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> to the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> to the southeast.
</p><p>The sea stretches nearly 1,200 kilometres (750 mi) from north to south, with an average width of 320 km (200 mi). Its gross coverage is 386,400 km<sup>2</sup> (149,200 sq mi) and the surface is about 27 m (89 ft) below <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. Its main freshwater <a href="/wiki/Inflow_(hydrology)" title="Inflow (hydrology)">inflow</a>, Europe's longest river, the <a href="/wiki/Volga" title="Volga">Volga</a>, enters at the shallow north end. Two deep basins form its central and southern zones. These lead to horizontal differences in temperature, salinity, and ecology. The <a href="/wiki/Seabed" title="Seabed">seabed</a> in the south reaches 1,023 m (3,356 ft) below sea level, which is the second-lowest natural non-oceanic <a href="/wiki/Depression_(geology)" title="Depression (geology)">depression</a> on Earth after <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a> (−1,180 m or −3,870 ft). Written accounts from the ancient inhabitants of its coast perceived the Caspian Sea as an ocean, probably because of its salinity and large size.
</p><p>The Caspian Sea is home to a wide range of species and is known for its <a href="/wiki/Caviar" title="Caviar">caviar</a> and oil industries. Pollution from the oil industry and dams on rivers draining into it have harmed its ecology.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The lake's name stems from <a href="/wiki/Caspians" title="Caspians">Caspi</a>, an ancient people who lived to the southwest of the sea in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> (died circa AD 24) wrote that "to the country of the Albanians (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caucasus_Albania" title="Caucasus Albania">Caucasus Albania</a> not to be confused with the country of <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>) belongs also the territory called Caspiane, which was named after the Caspian tribe, as was also the sea; but the tribe has now disappeared".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Moreover, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caspian_Gates" title="Caspian Gates">Caspian Gates</a>, part of <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Tehran_province" title="Tehran province">Tehran province</a>, may evince such a people migrated to the south. The Iranian city of <a href="/wiki/Qazvin" title="Qazvin">Qazvin</a> shares the root of its name with this common name for the sea. The traditional and medieval  Arabic name for the sea was  Bahr(sea) Xazar but in recent centuries common and standard name in Arabic language is Baḥr <a href="/wiki/Qazvin" title="Qazvin">Qazvin</a> Arabized from Caspian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>  In modern <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Каспи́йское мо́ре</span>, <i>Kaspiyskoye more</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LPIran_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-LPIran-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some Turkic ethnic groups refer to it with the Caspi(an) descriptor; in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kazakh_Language" title="Kazakh Language">Kazakh</a> it is called <span title="Kazakh-language text"><span lang="kk">Каспий теңізі</span></span>, <i>Kaspiy teñizi</i>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a>: <span lang="ky">Каспий деңизи</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Kyrgyz" title="Romanization of Kyrgyz">romanized</a>: </small><span title="Kyrgyz-language romanization"><i lang="ky-Latn">Kaspiy deñizi</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>: <span lang="uz">Kaspiy dengizi</span>.  Others refer to it as the <i>Khazar sea</i>: <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>: <i lang="tk">Hazar deňizi</i>; <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>: <i lang="az">Xəzər dənizi</i>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Hazar denizi</i>. In all these the first word refers to the historical <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a> who had a large empire based to the north of the Caspian Sea between the 7th and 10th centuries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In Iran, the lake is referred to as the <i>Mazandaran Sea</i> (<a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: <i dir="rtl" lang="fa-Latn">دریای مازندران</i>), after the historic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mazandaran_Province" title="Mazandaran Province">Mazandaran Province</a> at its southern shores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Old Russian sources use the <i>Khvalyn</i> or <i>Khvalis</i> Sea (<span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Хвалынское море / Хвалисское море</span></span>) after the name of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khwarezmia" title="Khwarezmia">Khwarezmia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Among Greeks and Persians in <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a> it was the <a href="/wiki/Hyrcania" title="Hyrcania">Hyrcanian</a> ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Renaissance European maps labelled it as the <i>Abbacuch Sea</i> (Oronce Fine's 1531 world map), <i>Mar de <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Bachu</a></i> (Ortellius' 1570 map), or <i>Mar de Sala</i> (Mercator's 1569 map).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Basin_countries">Basin countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Basin countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_countries">Border countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Border countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-border_countries">Non-border countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Non-border countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> (entirety)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> (its east part)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (extreme north-eastern parts)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> (extreme western parts)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_characteristics">Physical characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Physical characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation">Formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Caspian Sea, like the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, is a remnant of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Paratethys" title="Paratethys">Paratethys Sea</a>. Its seafloor is, therefore, a standard oceanic <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a> and not a continental <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> body. It became landlocked about 5.5 million years ago due to <a href="/wiki/Tectonic_uplift" title="Tectonic uplift">tectonic uplift</a> and a fall in <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. During warm and dry climatic periods, the landlocked sea almost dried up, depositing <a href="/wiki/Evaporite" title="Evaporite">evaporitic sediments</a> like <a href="/wiki/Halite" title="Halite">halite</a> that were covered by wind-blown deposits and were sealed off as an <a href="/wiki/Evaporite" title="Evaporite">evaporite</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sink_(geography)" title="Sink (geography)">sink</a> when cool, wet climates refilled the basin. (Comparable evaporite beds underlie the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a>.) Due to the current inflow of fresh water in the north, the Caspian Sea water is almost fresh in its northern portions, getting more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brackish" title="Brackish">brackish</a> toward the south. It is most saline on the Iranian shore, where the catchment basin contributes little flow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Currently, the mean salinity of the Caspian is one third that of Earth's oceans. The <a href="/wiki/Garabogazk%C3%B6l" title="Garabogazköl">Garabogazköl</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embayment" title="Embayment">embayment</a>, which dried up when water flow from the main body of the Caspian was blocked in the 1980s but has since been restored, routinely exceeds oceanic salinity by a factor of 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web1_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-web1-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CaspianSeaDrainage_v1.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="966" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CaspianSeaDrainage_v1.png/220px-CaspianSeaDrainage_v1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CaspianSeaDrainage_v1.png/330px-CaspianSeaDrainage_v1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CaspianSeaDrainage_v1.png/440px-CaspianSeaDrainage_v1.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CaspianSeaDrainage_v1.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Area around the Caspian Sea. Yellow area indicates the (approximate) drainage area.</div></div></div>
<p>The Caspian Sea is the largest inland body of water in the world by area and accounts for 40 to 44% of the total <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lacustrine" title="wikt:lacustrine">lacustrine</a> waters of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-irngaz_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-irngaz-15">[15]</a></sup>, and covers an area larger than <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>.  The coastlines of the Caspian are shared by <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, Iran, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, Russia, and <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>. The Caspian is divided into three distinct physical regions: the Northern, Middle, and Southern Caspian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hooshang1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-hooshang1-16">[16]</a></sup> The Northern–Middle boundary is the <a href="/wiki/Mangyshlak_Peninsula" title="Mangyshlak Peninsula">Mangyshlak</a> Threshold, which runs through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chechen_Island" title="Chechen Island">Chechen Island</a> and Cape Tiub-Karagan. The Middle–Southern boundary is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apsheron_Threshold" title="Apsheron Threshold">Apsheron Threshold</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Aquatic_sill" title="Aquatic sill">sill</a> of tectonic origin between the Eurasian continent and an oceanic remnant,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> that runs through Zhiloi Island and Cape Kuuli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dumont1_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-dumont1-18">[18]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Garabogazk%C3%B6l" title="Garabogazköl">Garabogazköl</a> Bay is the saline eastern inlet of the Caspian, which is part of Turkmenistan and at times has been a lake in its own right due to the isthmus that cuts it off from the Caspian.
</p><p>Differences between the three regions are dramatic. The Northern Caspian only includes the Caspian shelf,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kost1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-kost1-19">[19]</a></sup> and is very shallow; it accounts for less than 1% of the total water volume with an average depth of only 5–6 metres (16–20 ft). The sea noticeably drops off towards the Middle Caspian, where the average depth is 190 metres (620 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dumont1_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-dumont1-18">[18]</a></sup> The Southern Caspian is the deepest, with oceanic depths of over 1,000 metres (3,300 ft), greatly exceeding the depth of other regional seas, such as the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>. The Middle and Southern Caspian account for 33% and 66% of the total water volume, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hooshang1_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-hooshang1-16">[16]</a></sup> The northern portion of the Caspian Sea typically freezes in the winter, and in the coldest winters ice forms in the south as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>
Over 130 rivers provide inflow to the Caspian, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a> being the largest. A second affluent, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a>, flows in from the north, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kura_(Caspian_Sea)" title="Kura (Caspian Sea)">Kura River</a> from the west. In the past, the <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amu Darya</a> (Oxus) of Central Asia in the east often changed course to empty into the Caspian through a now-desiccated riverbed called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uzboy_River" title="Uzboy River">Uzboy River</a>, as did the <a href="/wiki/Syr_Darya" title="Syr Darya">Syr Darya</a> farther north. The Caspian has several small islands, primarily located in the north with a collective land area of roughly 2,000 km<sup>2</sup> (770 sq mi). Adjacent to the North Caspian is the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Depression" title="Caspian Depression">Caspian Depression</a>, a low-lying region 27 metres (89 ft) below <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asian</a> <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a> stretch across the northeast coast, while the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Caucasus" title="Greater Caucasus">Caucasus mountains</a> hug the western shore. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomes" title="Biomes">biomes</a> to both the north and east are characterized by cold, continental deserts. Conversely, the climate to the southwest and south are generally warm with uneven elevation due to a mix of highlands and <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain ranges</a>; the drastic changes in climate alongside the Caspian have led to a great deal of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web1_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-web1-14">[14]</a></sup></p><div style="clear:left;"></div>
<p>The Caspian Sea has numerous islands near the coasts, but none in the deeper parts of the sea. <a href="/wiki/Ogurja_Ada" title="Ogurja Ada">Ogurja Ada</a> is the largest island. The island is 37 km (23 mi) long, with <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">gazelles</a> roaming freely on it. In the North Caspian, the majority of the islands are small and uninhabited, like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tyuleniy_Archipelago_(Kazakhstan)" title="Tyuleniy Archipelago (Kazakhstan)">Tyuleniy Archipelago</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Important_Bird_Area" title="Important Bird Area">Important Bird Area</a> (IBA).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The climate of the Caspian Sea is variable, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_desert_climate" title="Cold desert climate">cold desert climate</a> (BWk), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" title="Cold semi-arid climate">cold semi-arid climate</a> (BSk), and <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (Dsa, Dfa) being present in the northern portions of the Caspian Sea, while the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (Csa) and <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (Cfa) are present in the southern portions of the Caspian Sea.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">Hydrology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hydrology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caspian_Sea_Kazakhstan_Mangistau.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="828" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Caspian_Sea_Kazakhstan_Mangistau.jpg/220px-Caspian_Sea_Kazakhstan_Mangistau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Caspian_Sea_Kazakhstan_Mangistau.jpg/330px-Caspian_Sea_Kazakhstan_Mangistau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Caspian_Sea_Kazakhstan_Mangistau.jpg/440px-Caspian_Sea_Kazakhstan_Mangistau.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caspian_Sea_Kazakhstan_Mangistau.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caspian Sea near <a href="/wiki/Aktau" title="Aktau">Aktau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mangystau_Region" title="Mangystau Region">Mangystau Region</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Caspian has characteristics common to both seas and lakes. It is often listed as the world's largest lake, although it is not <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater">freshwater</a>: the 1.2% salinity classes it with <a href="/wiki/Brackish_water" title="Brackish water">brackish water</a> bodies.
</p><p>It contains about 3.5 times as much water, by volume, as all five of North America's <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> combined. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a> (about 80% of the inflow) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a> discharge into the Caspian Sea, but it has no natural outflow other than by <a href="/wiki/Evaporation" title="Evaporation">evaporation</a>. Thus the Caspian <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Closed_basin" title="Closed basin">closed basin</a>, with its own sea level history that is independent of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eustasis" title="Eustasis">eustatic</a> level of the world's oceans.
</p><p>The sea level of the Caspian has fallen and risen, often rapidly, many times over the centuries. Some Russian historians<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2011)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> claim that a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval" title="Medieval">medieval</a> rising of the Caspian, perhaps caused by the <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amu Darya</a> changing its inflow to the Caspian from the 13th century to the 16th century, caused the coastal towns of <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazaria</a>, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atil,_Khazaria" title="Atil, Khazaria">Atil</a>, to flood. In 2004, the water level was 28 metres (92 feet) below <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>.
</p><p>Over the centuries, Caspian Sea levels have changed in synchrony with the estimated discharge of the Volga, which in turn depends on rainfall levels in its vast catchment basin. Precipitation is related to variations in the amount of North Atlantic depressions that reach the interior, and they in turn are affected by cycles of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_oscillation" title="North Atlantic oscillation">North Atlantic oscillation</a>. Thus levels in the Caspian Sea relate to atmospheric conditions in the North Atlantic, thousands of kilometres to the northwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>The last short-term sea-level cycle started with a sea-level fall of 3 m (10 ft) from 1929 to 1977, followed by a rise of 3 m (10 ft) from 1977 until 1995. Since then smaller oscillations have taken place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>A study by the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Azerbaijan National Academy of Sciences">Azerbaijan Academy of Sciences</a> estimated that the level of the sea was dropping by more than six centimetres per year due to increased evaporation due to rising temperatures caused by <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nation-20190418_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nation-20190418-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_degradation">Environmental degradation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environmental degradation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a>, the longest river in Europe, drains 20% of the European land area and is the source of 80% of the Caspian's inflow. Heavy development in its lower reaches has caused numerous unregulated releases of chemical and biological pollutants. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Environment_Programme" title="UN Environment Programme">UN Environment Programme</a> warns that the Caspian "suffers from an enormous burden of pollution from oil extraction and refining, offshore oil fields, radioactive wastes from nuclear power plants and huge volumes of untreated sewage and industrial waste introduced mainly by the Volga River".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nation-20190418_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nation-20190418-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>The magnitude of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a> extraction and transport activity in the Caspian also poses a risk to the environment. The island of <a href="/wiki/Vulf" title="Vulf">Vulf</a> off <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, for example, has suffered ecological damage as a result of the petrochemical industry; this has significantly decreased the number of species of marine birds in the area. Existing and planned oil and gas pipelines under the sea further increase the potential threat to the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>The high concentration of <a href="/wiki/Mud_volcano" title="Mud volcano">mud volcanoes</a> under the Caspian Sea were thought to be the cause of a fire that broke out 75 kilometers from <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> on July 5, 2021. The State oil company of Azerbaijan <a href="/wiki/SOCAR" title="SOCAR">SOCAR</a> said preliminary information indicated it was a mud volcano which spewed both mud and flammable gas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>It is assumed that during the 21st century, the level will decrease by 9–18 m (30–60 ft) due to the acceleration of evaporation due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> and the process of <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 23, 2021, Kazakhstan President <a href="/wiki/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev" title="Kassym-Jomart Tokayev">Kassym-Jomart Tokayev</a> signed the Protocol for the Protection of the Caspian Sea against Pollution from Land-based Sources in order to ensure better protection for the biodiversity of the Caspian Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ghaleye_Rud_Khan_(40)_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Ghaleye_Rud_Khan_%2840%29_4.jpg/220px-Ghaleye_Rud_Khan_%2840%29_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Ghaleye_Rud_Khan_%2840%29_4.jpg/330px-Ghaleye_Rud_Khan_%2840%29_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Ghaleye_Rud_Khan_%2840%29_4.jpg/440px-Ghaleye_Rud_Khan_%2840%29_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ghaleye_Rud_Khan_(40)_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iran's northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caspian_Hyrcanian_mixed_forests" title="Caspian Hyrcanian mixed forests">Caspian Hyrcanian mixed forests</a> are maintained by moisture captured from the Caspian Sea by the <a href="/wiki/Alborz" title="Alborz">Alborz Mountain Range</a>.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The rising level of the Caspian Sea between 1994 and 1996 reduced the number of habitats for rare species of aquatic vegetation. This has been attributed to a general lack of seeding material in newly formed coastal <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoons</a> and water bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many rare and endemic plant species of Russia are associated with the <a href="/wiki/Intertidal_zone" title="Intertidal zone">tidal areas</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volga_delta" title="Volga delta">Volga delta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Riparian_forest" title="Riparian forest">riparian forests</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samur_River" title="Samur River">Samur River</a> delta. The shoreline is also a unique refuge for plants adapted to the loose sands of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_northern_desert" title="Central Asian northern desert">Central Asian Deserts</a>. The principal limiting factors to successful establishment of plant species are hydrological imbalances within the surrounding deltas, <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>, and various land reclamation activities. The water level change within the Caspian Sea is an indirect reason for which plants may not get established.
</p><p>These affect aquatic plants of the Volga Delta, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Aldrovanda_vesiculosa" title="Aldrovanda vesiculosa">Aldrovanda vesiculosa</a></i> and the native <i><a href="/wiki/Nelumbo" title="Nelumbo">Nelumbo caspica</a></i>. About 11 plant species are found in the Samur River delta, including the unique <a href="/wiki/Liana" title="Liana">liana</a> forests that date back to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tertiary_period" title="Tertiary period">Tertiary period</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2019 <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> has admitted the lush <a href="/wiki/Hyrcanian_forests" title="Hyrcanian forests">Hyrcanian forests</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mazandaran" title="Mazandaran">Mazandaran</a>, Iran as World Heritage Site under category (ix). <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Benthophilus_granulosus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1348" data-file-width="2204" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Benthophilus_granulosus.jpg/220px-Benthophilus_granulosus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Benthophilus_granulosus.jpg/330px-Benthophilus_granulosus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Benthophilus_granulosus.jpg/440px-Benthophilus_granulosus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benthophilus_granulosus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Most <a href="/wiki/Tadpole_goby" title="Tadpole goby">tadpole gobies</a> (<i>Benthophilus</i>) are only found in the Caspian Sea basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Caspian_turtle" title="Caspian turtle">Caspian turtle</a> (<i>Mauremys caspica</i>), although found in neighboring areas, is a wholly freshwater species. The <a href="/wiki/Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel">zebra mussel</a> is native to the Caspian and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> basins, but has become an <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive species</a> elsewhere, when introduced. The area has given its name to several species, including the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_gull" title="Caspian gull">Caspian gull</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_tern" title="Caspian tern">Caspian tern</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Caspian_seal" title="Caspian seal">Caspian seal</a> (<i>Pusa caspica</i>) is the only aquatic mammal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endemic_(ecology)" title="Endemic (ecology)">endemic</a> to the Caspian Sea, being one of very few <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seal species</a> that live in inland waters, but it is different from the <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_seal" title="Freshwater seal">those inhabiting freshwaters</a> due to the hydrological environment of the sea. A century ago the Caspian was home to more than one million <a href="/wiki/Caspian_seal" title="Caspian seal">seals</a>. Today, fewer than 10% remain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nation-20190418_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Nation-20190418-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>Archeological studies of <a href="/wiki/Gobustan_Rock_Art" title="Gobustan Rock Art">Gobustan Rock Art</a> have identified what may be <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Porpoise" title="Porpoise">porpoises</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> or a certain species of <a href="/wiki/Beaked_whale" title="Beaked whale">beaked whale</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gallagher_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gallagher-36">[36]</a></sup> and what may be a whaling scene indicates large <a href="/wiki/Baleen_whale" title="Baleen whale">baleen whales</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gallagher2_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gallagher2-37">[37]</a></sup> likely being present in the Caspian Sea at least until it ceased being a part of the ocean system or until the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> or much more recent periods such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">antiquity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Although the rock art on <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kichikdash_Mountain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kichikdash Mountain (page does not exist)">Kichikdash Mountain</a> is assumed to be of a dolphin<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GH_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-GH-39">[39]</a></sup> or of a beaked whale,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gallagher_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gallagher-36">[36]</a></sup> it might instead represent the famous <a href="/wiki/Beluga_(sturgeon)" title="Beluga (sturgeon)">beluga sturgeon</a> due to its size (430 cm in length), but fossil records suggest certain ancestors of modern dolphins and whales, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Kentriodontidae" title="Kentriodontidae">Macrokentriodon</a> morani</i> (<a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">bottlenose dolphins</a>) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balaenoptera_sibbaldina" title="Balaenoptera sibbaldina">Balaenoptera sibbaldina</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Blue_whale" title="Blue whale">blue whales</a>) were presumably larger than their present descendants. From the same artworks, <a href="/wiki/Auk" title="Auk">auks</a>, like <a href="/wiki/Thick-billed_murre" title="Thick-billed murre">Brunnich's Guillemot</a> could also have been in the sea as well, and these petroglyphs suggest marine inflow between the current Caspian Sea and the Arctic Ocean or <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GH_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-GH-39">[39]</a></sup> This is supported by the existences of current endemic, oceanic species such as <a href="/wiki/Cerastoderma_glaucum" title="Cerastoderma glaucum">lagoon cockles</a> which was genetically identified to originate in Caspian/Black Seas regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gallagher2_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gallagher2-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>The sea's <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">basin</a> (including associated waters such as rivers) has 160 native species and <a href="/wiki/Subspecies" title="Subspecies">subspecies</a> of fish in more than 60 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genera" title="Genera">genera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup> About 62% of the species and subspecies are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>, as are 4–6 genera (depending on <a href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(biology)" title="Taxonomy (biology)">taxonomic</a> treatment). The lake proper has 115 natives, including 73 endemics (63.5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup> Among the more than 50 genera in the lake proper, 3–4 are endemic: <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatirostrum" title="Anatirostrum">Anatirostrum</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caspiomyzon" title="Caspiomyzon">Caspiomyzon</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ponticola_bathybius" title="Ponticola bathybius">Chasar</a></i> (often included in <i><a href="/wiki/Ponticola" title="Ponticola">Ponticola</a></i>) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyrcanogobius" title="Hyrcanogobius">Hyrcanogobius</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup> By far the most numerous families in the lake proper are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gobies" title="Gobies">gobies</a> (35 species and subspecies), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyprinid" title="Cyprinid">cyprinids</a> (32) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clupeid" title="Clupeid">clupeids</a> (22). Two particularly rich genera are <i><a href="/wiki/Alosa" title="Alosa">Alosa</a></i> with 18 endemic species/subspecies and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benthophilus" title="Benthophilus">Benthophilus</a></i> with 16 endemic species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup> Other examples of endemics are four species of <i><a href="/wiki/Clupeonella" title="Clupeonella">Clupeonella</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gobio_volgensis" title="Gobio volgensis">Gobio volgensis</a></i>, two <i><a href="/wiki/Rutilus" title="Rutilus">Rutilus</a></i>, three <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sabanejewia" title="Sabanejewia">Sabanejewia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Stenodus_leucichthys" title="Stenodus leucichthys">Stenodus leucichthys</a></i>, two <i><a href="/wiki/Salmo" title="Salmo">Salmo</a></i>, two <i><a href="/wiki/Mesogobius" title="Mesogobius">Mesogobius</a></i> and three <i><a href="/wiki/Neogobius" title="Neogobius">Neogobius</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-5"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup> Most non-endemic natives are either shared with the Black Sea basin or widespread <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palearctic" title="Palearctic">Palearctic</a> species such as <a href="/wiki/Crucian_carp" title="Crucian carp">crucian carp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prussian_carp" title="Prussian carp">Prussian carp</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_carp" title="Common carp">common carp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_bream" title="Common bream">common bream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_bleak" title="Common bleak">common bleak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asp_(fish)" title="Asp (fish)">asp</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_bream" title="White bream">white bream</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunbleak" title="Sunbleak">sunbleak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_dace" title="Common dace">common dace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_roach" title="Common roach">common roach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_rudd" title="Common rudd">common rudd</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_chub" title="European chub">European chub</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pelecus_cultratus" title="Pelecus cultratus">sichel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tench" title="Tench">tench</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_weatherfish" title="European weatherfish">European weatherfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wels_catfish" title="Wels catfish">wels catfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_pike" title="Northern pike">northern pike</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burbot" title="Burbot">burbot</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_perch" title="European perch">European perch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zander" title="Zander">zander</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-6"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup> Almost 30 non-indigenous, <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">introduced</a> fish species have been reported from the Caspian Sea, but only a few have become established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-7"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>Six <a href="/wiki/Sturgeon" title="Sturgeon">sturgeon</a> species, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_sturgeon" title="Russian sturgeon">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bastard_sturgeon" title="Bastard sturgeon">bastard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_sturgeon" title="Persian sturgeon">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sterlet" title="Sterlet">sterlet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starry_sturgeon" title="Starry sturgeon">starry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beluga_(sturgeon)" title="Beluga (sturgeon)">beluga</a>, are native to the Caspian Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naseka2009_32-8"><a href="#cite_note-Naseka2009-32">[32]</a></sup> The last of these is arguably the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_fish" title="List of largest fish">largest freshwater fish in the world</a>. The sturgeon yield <a href="/wiki/Roe" title="Roe">roe</a> (eggs) that are processed into <a href="/wiki/Caviar" title="Caviar">caviar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">Overfishing</a> has depleted a number of the historic fisheries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In recent years, overfishing has threatened the sturgeon population to the point that <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalists</a> advocate banning sturgeon fishing completely until the population recovers. The high price of sturgeon caviar—more than 1,500 <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_manat" title="Azerbaijani manat">Azerbaijani manats</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nation-20190418_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-Nation-20190418-23">[23]</a></sup> (US$880 as of April 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) per kilo—allows fishermen to afford bribes to ensure the authorities look the other way, making regulations in many locations ineffective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-41">[41]</a></sup> Caviar harvesting further endangers the fish stocks, since it targets reproductive females.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Extantigerturanianwksciam97.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="293" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Extantigerturanianwksciam97.jpg/220px-Extantigerturanianwksciam97.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Extantigerturanianwksciam97.jpg/330px-Extantigerturanianwksciam97.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Extantigerturanianwksciam97.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Extantigerturanianwksciam97.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration of two <a href="/wiki/Caspian_tiger" title="Caspian tiger">Caspian tigers</a>, extinct in the region since the 1970s.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">Reptiles</a> native to the region include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spur-thighed_tortoise" title="Spur-thighed tortoise">spur-thighed tortoise</a> (<i>Testudo graeca buxtoni</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Russian_tortoise" title="Russian tortoise">Horsfield's tortoise</a>.
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_cheetah" title="Asiatic cheetah">Asiatic cheetah</a> used to occur in the Trans-Caucasus and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, but is today restricted to Iran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geptner1972_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geptner1972-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humphreys1999_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Humphreys1999-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_lion" title="Asiatic lion">Asiatic lion</a> used to occur in the Trans-Caucasus, Iran, and possibly the southern part of <a href="/wiki/Turkestan" title="Turkestan">Turkestan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geptner1972_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-Geptner1972-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humphreys1999_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Humphreys1999-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Caspian_tiger" title="Caspian tiger">Caspian tiger</a> used to occur in northern Iran, the Caucasus and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geptner1972_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-Geptner1972-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humphreys1999_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-Humphreys1999-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>The endangered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_leopard" title="Persian leopard">Persian leopard</a> is found in Iran, the Caucasus and Central Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geptner1972_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-Geptner1972-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humphreys1999_43-3"><a href="#cite_note-Humphreys1999-43">[43]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bowen,_Emanuel;_Orbeliani,_Sulxan-Saba._A_new_and_accurate_map_of_the_Caspian_Sea._1747._(A).jpg"><img alt="A map of the Caspian Sea in the mid-1700s" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3064" data-file-width="2125" decoding="async" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Bowen%2C_Emanuel%3B_Orbeliani%2C_Sulxan-Saba._A_new_and_accurate_map_of_the_Caspian_Sea._1747._%28A%29.jpg/170px-Bowen%2C_Emanuel%3B_Orbeliani%2C_Sulxan-Saba._A_new_and_accurate_map_of_the_Caspian_Sea._1747._%28A%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Bowen%2C_Emanuel%3B_Orbeliani%2C_Sulxan-Saba._A_new_and_accurate_map_of_the_Caspian_Sea._1747._%28A%29.jpg/255px-Bowen%2C_Emanuel%3B_Orbeliani%2C_Sulxan-Saba._A_new_and_accurate_map_of_the_Caspian_Sea._1747._%28A%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Bowen%2C_Emanuel%3B_Orbeliani%2C_Sulxan-Saba._A_new_and_accurate_map_of_the_Caspian_Sea._1747._%28A%29.jpg/340px-Bowen%2C_Emanuel%3B_Orbeliani%2C_Sulxan-Saba._A_new_and_accurate_map_of_the_Caspian_Sea._1747._%28A%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bowen,_Emanuel;_Orbeliani,_Sulxan-Saba._A_new_and_accurate_map_of_the_Caspian_Sea._1747._(A).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A New and Accurate Map of the Caspian Sea by the Soskam Sabbus &amp; <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Bowen" title="Emanuel Bowen">Emanuel Bowen</a>, 1747.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caspian_sea_Ibn_Hawqal.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1846" data-file-width="1435" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Caspian_sea_Ibn_Hawqal.JPG/170px-Caspian_sea_Ibn_Hawqal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Caspian_sea_Ibn_Hawqal.JPG/255px-Caspian_sea_Ibn_Hawqal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Caspian_sea_Ibn_Hawqal.JPG/340px-Caspian_sea_Ibn_Hawqal.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caspian_sea_Ibn_Hawqal.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caspian Sea (Bahr ul-Khazar). 10th century map by Ibn Hawqal</div></div></div><p>The main geologic history locally had two stages. The first is the <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a>, determined by <a href="/wiki/Tectonics" title="Tectonics">tectonic</a> events that correlate with the closing of the <a href="/wiki/Tethys_Ocean" title="Tethys Ocean">Tethys Sea</a>. The second is the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> noted for its <a href="/wiki/Glacial_period" title="Glacial period">glaciation</a> cycles and the full run of the present Volga. During the first stage, the Tethys Sea had evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Sarmatians" title="Sarmatians">Sarmatian</a> Lake, that was created from the modern Black Sea and south Caspian, when the collision of the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian peninsula</a> with <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> pushed up the <a href="/wiki/Kopet_Dag" title="Kopet Dag">Kopet Dag</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a>, lasting south and west limits to the basin. This <a href="/wiki/Orogeny" title="Orogeny">orogeneic</a> movement was continuous, while the Caspian was regularly disconnected from the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. In the late Pontian, a mountain arch rose across the south basin and divided it into the <a href="/wiki/Khachmaz_District" title="Khachmaz District">Khachmaz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lankaran" title="Lankaran">Lankaran</a> Lakes (or early <a href="/wiki/Balaxan%C4%B1" title="Balaxanı">Balaxani</a>). The period of restriction to the south basin was reversed during the Akchagylian – the lake became more than three times its size today and took again the first of a series of contacts with the Black Sea and with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Aral" title="Lake Aral">Lake Aral</a>. A recession of Lake Akchagyl completed stage one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Surikov1906.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1047" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Surikov1906.jpg/220px-Surikov1906.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Surikov1906.jpg/330px-Surikov1906.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Surikov1906.jpg/440px-Surikov1906.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Surikov1906.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossack</a> rebel and pirate <a href="/wiki/Stenka_Razin" title="Stenka Razin">Stenka Razin</a>, on a raid in the Caspian (<a href="/wiki/Vasily_Surikov" title="Vasily Surikov">Vasily Surikov</a>, 1906)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_settlement_nearby">Early settlement nearby</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Early settlement nearby">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The earliest hominid remains found around the Caspian Sea are from <a href="/wiki/Dmanisi" title="Dmanisi">Dmanisi</a> dating back to around 1.8 Ma and yielded a number of skeletal remains of <a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a> or <a href="/wiki/Homo_ergaster" title="Homo ergaster">Homo ergaster</a>. More later evidence for human occupation of the region came from a number of caves in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> and Azerbaijan such as Kudaro and <a href="/wiki/Azykh_Cave" title="Azykh Cave">Azykh Caves</a>. There is evidence for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Palaeolithic" title="Lower Palaeolithic">Lower Palaeolithic</a> human occupation south of the Caspian from western Alburz. These are Ganj Par and <a href="/wiki/Darband_Cave" title="Darband Cave">Darband Cave</a> sites.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> remains also have been discovered at a cave in Georgia. Discoveries in the Hotu cave and the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Hotu_and_Kamarband_Caves" title="Hotu and Kamarband Caves">Kamarband cave</a>, near the town of <a href="/wiki/Behshahr" title="Behshahr">Behshahr</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mazandaran" title="Mazandaran">Mazandaran</a> south of the Caspian in Iran, suggest human habitation of the area as early as 11,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Ancient Greeks focused on the civilization on the south shore – they call it the (H)yr(c/k)anian Sea (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" title="Ancient Greek language">Ancient Greek</a>: <span lang="grc">Υρκανία θάλαττα</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> with sources noting the latter word was evolving then to today's <i>Thelessa</i>: late <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" title="Ancient Greek language">Ancient Greek</a>: <span lang="grc">θάλασσα</span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_maximal_limit">Chinese maximal limit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Chinese maximal limit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Later, in the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a> (618-907), the sea was the western limit of the Chinese Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tang1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tang1-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tang2_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tang2-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fossil_fuel">Fossil fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Fossil fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The area is rich in fossil fuels. Oil wells were being dug in the region as early as the 10th century to reach oil "for use in everyday life, both for medicinal purposes and for heating and lighting in homes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOCAR1_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-SOCAR1-51">[51]</a></sup> By the 16th century, Europeans were aware of the rich oil and gas deposits locally. English traders <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bannister" title="Thomas Bannister">Thomas Bannister</a> and Jeffrey Duckett described the area around <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> as "a strange thing to behold, for there issueth out of the ground a marvelous quantity of oil, which serveth all the country to burn in their houses. This oil is black and is called <a href="/wiki/Naphtha#Etymology" title="Naphtha">nefte</a>. There is also by the town of Baku, another kind of oil which is white and very precious [i.e., <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>]."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOCAR2_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-SOCAR2-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Today, oil and gas platforms abound along the edges of the sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Geography.2C_geology_and_navigation_studies"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography,_geology_and_navigation_studies">Geography, geology and navigation studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Geography, geology and navigation studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the rule of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_I_the_Great" title="Peter I the Great">Peter I the Great</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fedor_Ivanovich_Soimonov" title="Fedor Ivanovich Soimonov">Fedor I. Soimonov</a> was a pioneering explorer of the sea. He was a hydrographer who charted and greatly expanded knowledge of the sea. He drew a set of four maps and wrote <i>Pilot of the Caspian Sea</i>, the first lengthy report and modern maps. These were published in 1720 by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bak%C3%BC_gece_g%C3%B6r%C3%BCn%C3%BC%C5%9F%C3%BC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="392" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="84" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bak%C3%BC_gece_g%C3%B6r%C3%BCn%C3%BC%C5%9F%C3%BC.jpg/220px-Bak%C3%BC_gece_g%C3%B6r%C3%BCn%C3%BC%C5%9F%C3%BC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bak%C3%BC_gece_g%C3%B6r%C3%BCn%C3%BC%C5%9F%C3%BC.jpg/330px-Bak%C3%BC_gece_g%C3%B6r%C3%BCn%C3%BC%C5%9F%C3%BC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bak%C3%BC_gece_g%C3%B6r%C3%BCn%C3%BC%C5%9F%C3%BC.jpg/440px-Bak%C3%BC_gece_g%C3%B6r%C3%BCn%C3%BC%C5%9F%C3%BC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bak%C3%BC_gece_g%C3%B6r%C3%BCn%C3%BC%C5%9F%C3%BC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> is the largest city by the Caspian Sea.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ancient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hyrcania" title="Hyrcania">Hyrcania</a>, ancient state in the north of Iran</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sari,_Iran" title="Sari, Iran">Sari</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mazandaran_Province" title="Mazandaran Province">Mazandaran Province</a> of Iran</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bandar-e_Anzali" title="Bandar-e Anzali">Anzali</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gilan_Province" title="Gilan Province">Gilan Province</a> of Iran</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Astara,_Iran" title="Astara, Iran">Astara</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gilan_Province" title="Gilan Province">Gilan Province</a> of Iran</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astarabad" title="Astarabad">Astarabad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golestan_Province" title="Golestan Province">Golestan Province</a> of Iran</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sar_Kalateh-ye_Kharab_Shahr" title="Sar Kalateh-ye Kharab Shahr">Tamisheh</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golestan_Province" title="Golestan Province">Golestan Province</a> of Iran</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atil,_Khazaria" title="Atil, Khazaria">Atil, Khazaria</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Khazaran" title="Khazaran">Khazaran</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, Azerbaijan</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Derbent" title="Derbent">Derbent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dagestan" title="Dagestan">Dagestan</a>, Russia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xacitarxan" title="Xacitarxan">Xacitarxan</a>, modern-day <a href="/wiki/Astrakhan" title="Astrakhan">Astrakhan</a></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern">Modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D1%8E%D0%B6%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg"><img alt="" href="/wiki/Makhachkala" title="Makhachkala">Makhachkala</a>, the capital of the Russian republic of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Dagestan" title="Republic of Dagestan">Dagestan</a>, is the third-largest city on the Caspian Sea.</div></div></div>
